Dear Dr. Fannin NMA,
I would like to give you an update after our visit today. In an effort to keep unnecessary paperwork from
being generated, I am sending a short synopsis of my note. I would be happy to forward you a complete
note upon request.
ASSESSMENT/S:
eustachian tube dysfunction, headache, Chronic sinusitis, unspecified location, Postnasal drip, Perennial
allergic rhinitis, and lymphadenopathy
SUMMARY:
1-28-16 This is a very pleasant 39 year old who reports a long history of allergic rhinitis ever since
childhood. He has had adenotonsillectomy as well as at least 3 sets of tubes as a child also with no
significant ear infections as an adult. He does report intermittent paranasal headaches with frequent
nasal congestion and postnasal drainage and associated cough. He also has had intermittent swelling in
the region of his left parotid at times. On exam he has tympanosclerosis bilaterally without middle ear
effusion or inflammation, he has a mild septal deviation of left with allergic nasal findings and no acute
inflammation anteriorly or posteriorly on endoscopy, he has no suspicious lymphadenopathy and no
signs of parotid inflammation currently. He has had vision side effects with Flonase in the past so I
suggested a trial of Astelin as well as daily Zyrtec sinus rinses. He does have interest in allergy workup
and I can see him after this is completed.
I appreciate the opportunity to be involved with the care of this patient. Please feel free to contact me
with any questions - cell [PHONE-31].
Wes A. Allison. M.D.

Dear Dr. Fannin NMA,
I would like to give you an update after our visit today. In an effort to keep unnecessary paperwork from
being generated, I am sending a short synopsis of my note. I would be happy to forward you a complete
note upon request.
ASSESSMENT/S:
eustachian tube dysfunction, headache, Chronic sinusitis, unspecified location, Postnasal drip, Perennial
allergic rhinitis, and lymphadenopathy
SUMMARY:
[DOB-42] This is a very pleasant 40 year old who returns reporting worsening allergies over the past
year despite trials of Flonase and Zyrtec. He reports nasal trauma 2 months ago with a possible nasal
injury. On exam his nose is midline with no evidence of recent trauma, he continues to have a stable
septal deviation to the left with allergic nasal findings posteriorly and no acute inflammation on
endoscopy. He is agreeable allergy workup and I can see him after this is completed. We'll continue a
daily spray and antihistamine regimen otherwise.
I appreciate the opportunity to be involved with the care of this patient. Please feel free to contact me
with any questions - cell [PHONE-1144].

PATIENT:

[DOB-1186]
Dear Dr. Fannin NMA,
I would like to give you an update after our visit today. In an effort to keep unnecessary paperwork from
being generated, I am sending a short synopsis of my note. I would be happy to forward you a complete
note upon request.
ASSESSMENT/S:
eustachian tube dysfunction, headache, Chronic sinusitis, unspecified location, Postnasal drip, Perennial
allergic rhinitis, and lymphadenopathy
SUMMARY:
4/14/17-This is a very pleasant 40 year old who returns after allergy workup was performed and we
discussed these results in detail. His testing showed severe allergies across-the-board. He had mild
obstructive findings on spirometry. On exam, he has tympanosclerosis bilaterally without middle ear
effusion or inflammation, he has a stable septal deviation to the left without acute sinonasal
inflammation. We discussed the risks and benefits of immunotherapy and he will give this consideration
as he may be switching insurances soon. I suggested he start Claritin and Zyrtec in the meantime as our
test results can be used for up to one year should he wish to pursue immunotherapy. I can see him
again in six months to follow his progress or sooner for worsening symptoms. Of note, he was unable to
use Flonase due to side effects.

Assessment, Management and Plan:
45 yo male with transsphincteric anal fistula, state post seton placement 11/4.
Discussed in depth definitive repair of this, with illustrations.
Would like to do LIFT if possible, as both LIFT and ERAF have 65-70% success rate, and if recurs, presumably LIFT
should recur as intersphineteric allowing for sphincterotomy.
However, if his tract is as deep as I think it is, or perhaps even seems to go suprasphincteric, then will need to perform
ERAF. Both of these carry a small but present risk of incontinence - with his anal spasm and tone I think this is highly
unlikely.
Also discussed defecatory dysfunction - 1 think he will benefit from Pelvic Floor PT and he agrees. Discussed will work
on this postop after definitive repair of fistula.

Generated on 11/4/24 11:53 AM Page 65
Patient Name: Kiper,James
Date Of Birth: 4/29/1976
MRN: EP00479698
Norton Healthcare Telemedicine Informed Consent
I understand that telemedicine is the use of electronic information and communication technologies by a health care provider to
deliver services to an individual when he/she is located at a different site than the provider; and hereby consent to Norton
Healthcare providing health care services to me via telemedicine. The information discussed may be used for diagnosis, therapy,
follow-up and/or education.
Expected Benefits:
•Improved access to care by enabling a patient to obtain services from providers at distant sites.
•Patient remains closer to home where local healthcare providers can maintain continuity of care.
•Reduced need to travel for the patient or other provider.
The Process:
You will be introduced to the provider, such as residents, fellows, medical students and/or students of various health care fields who
are not employees of Norton Healthcare. You may ask questions of the provider or any telemedicine staff in the room with you, if you
are unsure of what is happening. If you are not comfortable with seeing a provider on videoconferencing technology, you may reject
the use of the technology and schedule a traditional face-to-face encounter at any time. Safety measures have been implemented to
ensure that this videoconference is secure, and no part of the encounter will be recorded without your written consent.
Possible Risks:
There are potential risks associated with the use of telemedicine which include, but may not be limited to:
•A provider may determine that the telehealth encounter is not yielding sufficient information to make an appropriate clinical
decision.
•Technology problems may delay medical evaluation and treatment for your encounter.
•In very rare instances, security protocols could fail, causing a breach of privacy of personal medical information.
By Signing this Form, I understand the following:
1 . I understand that the laws that protect privacy and confidentiality of medical information also apply to telemedicine, and that no
information obtained in the use of telemedicine which identifies me will be disclosed to researchers or other entities without my
consent.
2. I understand that l have the right to withdraw my consent to the use of telemedicine in the course of my care at any time, without
affecting my right to future care or treatment.
3. I also understand that if the provider believes I would be better served by a traditional face-to-face encounter, they may, at any
time stop the telemedicine visit and schedule a face-to-face visit.
4. I understand that l may expect the anticipated benefits from the use of telemedicine in my care, but that no results can be
guaranteed or assured.
Patient Consent to the Use of Telemedicine:
I have read and understand the information provided above regarding telemedicine, and all of my questions have been answered to
my satisfaction. I hereby give my informed consent for the use of telemedicine in my care.
I hereby authorize Norton Healthcare to use telemedicine in the course of my diagnosis and treatment.
self
12/05/23 2:30 PM

\rative-Proce\
)OI
prepped and draped in normal sterile fashion. I began by injecting 20 mL of
0.25% Marcaine, 1% lidocaine with epinephrine mixture into the ischiorectal
fat in the intersphincteric space for a local block. I then performed a
digital rectal exam low and posterior on the right side, there was an area of
rough regularity in the anal canal. I have been visualized this by inserting
a small and then a medium and then a large Sawyer retractor, to where 1 could
see some heaped up granulation tissue distal to the dentate line inside the
anal canal. 1 then injected hydrogen peroxide into the external opening,
which was approximately 5 cm away from the anal canal in the right posterior
direction. Hydrogen peroxide did come out inside the anal canal, confirming
presence of a fistulous tract.
I then took a fistula probe and very gently guided i t through fistula tract to
the area, where my finger could feel the probe coming through the area, where
the defect was internally. Of note, this tract went quite deep through the
ischiorectal fat before coming through the sphincters. I placed a silk tie
through the fistula probe, brought it out through the external opening and
then tied this to a vessel loop,which I then used in a rendezvous backward
type fashion to pull it back through the anal fistula and used a hemostat to
keep the ends of the vessel loop together. At this point,1 then tried to
make the fistula tract as short as possible. I extended the external opening
by making the incision with the Bovie approximately 1.5 cm closer to the anal
canal and curetted out the abscess cavity under the external opening
to help allow this to heal. I irrigated both the anal canal into die abscess
cavity with saline and assured hemostasis. At this point, I then tied the
seton together with a series of 3-0 silk ties in a teardrop configuration.
So, this would not completely turn inside the anal canal cause him pain and
blockage. At this point, finally before ending the procedure, I placed an
anal retractor back into the anal canal and thoroughly visualized exactly how
he is going to prepare for my second-stage. Given the depth of this fistula,
Ifeel that a lift would be quite difficult and he does have some anal mucosa
to perform an endorectal advancement flap, which was likely what he will need
at the second-stage once the inflammation goes down.
1 finished the procedure by injecting another 20 mL of local anesthesia into
the area around, where I did both a curette and the external opening
extension. I placed bacitracin over these wounds. 1also packed the cavity
around the external opening with a small amount of iodoform Nu Gauze. We then
placed clean sterile dressing. The patient was taken to recovery room in
satisfactory condition.

Operative Summary
PATIENT DOB:4/29/1976 DATE OF SURGERY: [DOB-880]
PREOPERATIVE DIAGNOSIS(ES): Transsphincteric anal fistula.
POSTOPERATIVE DIAGNOSIS(ES):
Transsphincteric anal fistula.
PROCEDURE PERFORMED: Exam under anesthesia, ligation of intersphincteric
fistula tract.
SURGEON: Sandra Kavalukas
ASSISTANT: Jonathon Vacek, MD, Resident.
ESTIMATED BLOOD LOSS: 10 mL.
ANESTHESIA: General endotracheal.
POSITION: Prone.
SPECIMENS: None.
INDICATIONS FOR OPERATION: This is a 45-year-old male who previously had a
seton placed for a somewhat deep tracking anal fistula that went through the
external and internal anal sphincters toward the tract went deep in the
Intersphincteric groove, however, then sharply curved back toward the lowlying internal opening. He had several weeks for the inflammation to resolve
and he is here for definitive repair.
PROCEDURE IN DETAIL: After informed consent was obtained, the patient was
taken back to the operating room. General endotracheal anesthesia was induced
on the stretcher. He was then placed in prone jack-knife position. His
perineum was prepped and draped in normal sterile fashion. A time-out was
performed. We then did a digital rectal exam where we can see some nodularity
and feel an internal opening just on the left posterolateral aspect of the
anal canal. He also had some granulation tissue from his previous fistulotomy
with an attempt to make that track shorter. I curetted this out to make that
wound base clean again. We then took a fistula probe and passed it through

Operative-Procedure Reports
the area where the seton was, again this was somewhat deep. However,I did
feel that I may be able to palpate and get down to this fistula tract, so we
started our intersphincteric incision. This was done in a linear fashion in
the intersphincteric groove, used the Lone Star retractor to help retract the
skin on the way, and then we gained access to the intersphincteric plane
without taking any external sphincter muscle. We bluntly dissected down with
a hemostat gently spreading until I was completely surrounded the fistula
tract, I grabbed this with a Kelly clamp and attempted to move both the seton
and the probe and we did indeed have the tract above us. At this point, we
passed two 2-0 Vicryl ties, tried to elongate the tract as much possible, cut
down with a 15 blade until we actually saw the metal for the fistula probe and
then backed the probe out. At this point,I took 2-0 Vicryl on UR-6 and tied
a figure-of-eight suture on both the internal and external side of this
fistula tract and then continued to divide it. We then went back behind that
using that as a handle and through several more throws of the 2-0 Vicryl
suture to completely close the fistula tract. We then tested this with
hydrogen peroxide from both the external opening side where there was no
leakage and then the internal opening side, we did still have some leakage, so
we continued to throw some more throws of the stitch until this was completely
tied down.
We then irrigated out this dissection plane, assured hemostasis, and the last
thing that we did before we started to close was to appose the ends of the
fistula tract. Therefore,I took a stitch through the superior aspect of the
internal opening area and tied this to the inferior aspect of the external
opening areas that we could offset these fistula tracts to be laid them from
just growing back together. We then closed the deep dermal stitch with a 3-0
Vicryl, closed the skin with 3-0 chromic, and left the curetted fistula area
out to be tacked. At this point, the patient was taken to the recovery room
in satisfactory condition.

PROCEDURE IN DETAIL:

operating room and placed supine on the operating room table. LMA anesthesia
was induced. He was placed in candy-cane lithotomy. Perineum was prepped and

prior to doing this,I performed digital rectal exam. The anal sphincter was
tight. However, overall, the mucosa felt healthy and most importantly, his
posterior midline anal fissure appeared to be markedly better healed. I
inserted a small and then very gingerly a medium Sawyer retractor and indeed
his anal fissure had healed quite a bit in the left side, where the seton was
and the left-sided external opening was very quiescent and appeared to be
healing well. We therefore turned our attention to incision and drainage of
the right-sided perianal abscess.
The Bovie electrocautery made a 2 cm incision in the point of maximum
fluctuance. Immediately he got out some purulent drainage,opened this
cavity up with the hemostats and irrigated this out. I did inject hydrogen
peroxide into the cavity to see if this would communicate over to the left
side and come out the area of the seton, however, it did not. I then next
placed the fistula probe into the cavity, which did track posteriorly toward
the coccyx, however, did not cross the midline or find any fistulous
connections or communications over to the left side. Because I was worried
about a blind and reforming abscess after the skin healed, I then placed a
seton subcutaneously through the deepest part of the tracking, but used this
only as a vessel loop to serve as a Penrose drain. We then irrigated out
again, assured hemostasis and packed the cavity with iodoform packing. The
patient was taken to recovery room in satisfactory condition.

Operative Summary
PATIENT DOB:4/29/ I 976 DATE OF SURGERY: [DOB-376]
PREOPERATIVE DIAGNOSIS(ES): Possible anal fistula.
POSTOPERATIVE DIAGNOSIS(ES): Possible anal fistula.
PROCEDURE PERFORMED: Exam under anesthesia with placement of subcutaneous
Ethibond seton and transsphincteric Ethihond seton.
SURGEON: Sandra Kavalukas
ASSISTANT: Mohammed I Ranavaya,MD.
SECONDARY SURGEON: Jeffrey Jorden, MD
ESTIMATED BLOOD LOSS: None.
ANESTHESIA: General endotracheal.
POSITIONING: C’andy-cane lithotomy.
IN'S AND OUTS: Per anesthetic care record.
SPECIMENS: None.
PROCEDURE IN DETAIL: After informed consent was obtained, the patient was
taken back to the operating room and placed supine on the operating room
table. General endotracheal anesthesia was induced. He was placed in
candy-cane lithotomy. His perineum was prepped and draped in normal sterile
fashion. Time-out was performed. We began by injecting 20 mL of 0,25%
Marcaine and 1% lidocaine with epinephrine in the ischiorectal fat in the
inlersphincteric space for perianal block. He had healed skin and some minor
drainage from the left posterolateral aspect where the seton was. 1 was able
to open this in the skin edge and injected hydrogen peroxide with the anal
retractor in the anal canal and did notsee hydrogen peroxide. We carefully
took a listula probe. We tracked further posteriorly and somewhat towards the
midline into an empty cavity and this was consistent with his complaints of
symptomatic pressure with occasional drainage. My thought at that point was

lo simply place a subcutaneous seton and see if this would continue to allow

continued to make a small counter incision to make a subcutaneousseton so
that, hopefully, in about a month, I can pull out the transsphincteric one and
leave the external subcutaneous one only to sec if this will heal up. At that
point, we injected more local anesthesia. The patient was taken to recovery
room in satisfactory condition.

General Information

that he had some mild bulging discs and they weren't enough to be causing the pain in the shouiders/arms.

 CONDITIONS OF ADMISSION AND 
AUTHORIZATION FOR TREATMENT □ Kosair Children's Hospital □ Norton Hospital □ Norton Audubon Hospital □ Norton Suburban Hospital □ Norton Brownsboro Hospital □ Kosair Children’s Medical Center
I. CONSENT TO DIAGNOSTIC TESTS, PROCEDURES, AND MEDICAL TREATMENT: 
I voluntarily consent to care that involves routine diagnostic tests, procedures, and medical treatment as prescribed by my physician and performed by the facility. No guarantee has been given by 
anyone as to the results that may be obtained. This consent includes testing for Hepatitis, Human Immunodeficiency Virus (HIV) or any other blood-borne infectious diseases, if ordered for diagnostic 
purposes or due to an occupational exposure. I consent to photographing, videotaping, video monitoring and audio devices for medical, scientific, safety or education purposes as well as for the 
purposes of identification. I understand that these will be stored in a secure manner that will protect my privacy. Images that identify me will only be released when authorized by me or as needed to 
provide for my continued medical treatment or identification.
II. OTHER PRACTITIONERS AND SUPPLIERS OF SERVICES:
I understand and acknowledge that I may require the services of physicians, groups of physicians or other practitioners (such as nurses and physician assistants) who are not employees of the hospital,
including, but not limited to, anesthesiologists, radiologists, emergency department physicians, certified registered nurse anesthetists, and other practitioners. I also understand that residents, fellows,
medical students, and students of various health care fields may be involved in my care and that they are not employees of the hospital. I agree that the signing of this document does not in any way
imply that Norton Healthcare is responsible for or assumes any liability for the activities of any such physicians or practitioners who are not its employees. When a physician, other practitioner or supplier of services bills me directly, I agree to pay the bill. I agree that the provisions regarding the release of information and assignment of benefits set out in paragraphs III and V below shall apply
not only to the hospital but also to such physicians, practitioners and suppliers of services and their claims for payment.
III. RELEASE OF INFORMATION:
I authorize the facility to notify my referring and treating physician(s), of my admission to the facility and to release any information about me as requested by such physician(s). I authorize the facility
and any other holder of medical or other information about me including medical information concerning drug related conditions, alcoholism, psychological conditions, psychiatric conditions, and/or
blood-borne infectious diseases, to release to the Social Security Administration, its intermediaries and its carriers, State agencies, the review organization employed by my employer, or the employer of
the insured member of my family, or any private third-party payor, as appropriate, any information required for the completion of any claim for benefits arising out of services rendered to me either on
an inpatient or outpatient basis. I further authorize the release of my social security number to the manufacturer of any implanted medical device in accordance with the Medical Device Tracking Act of
the Food and Drug Administration (FDA). I authorize the release of my HIV test results to healthcare personnel in the event of an occupational exposure. If my injury is work-related, I authorize the
facility and any other holder of medical or other information about me to release from my medical record any information as requested by the company and/or its workers compensation administrator as
indicated below:
COMPANY________________________________________________________________________ ADDRESS__________________________________________
IV. (initial)
THE FACILITY IS NOT RESPONSIBLE FOR LOSS OF PERSONAL ARTICLES:

V. ASSIGNMENT OF BENEFITS:
I agree to the assignment of all third-party benefits to the facility and agree to pay the facility for all charges not covered by third-party payors. In the case of outpatient services I agree that this 
document shall remain in full force and effect until specifically revoked by me in writing. Any sums not paid by a third-party payor are my obligation.
VI. RELEASE OF INSURANCE INFORMATION TO FACILITY:
I agree to the release by my insurance carrier to the facility and the facility's billing service of any eligibility and utilization data concerning my insurance coverage which the facility and/or its billing 
supplier may require.
VII. PAYMENT OF FACILITY BILLS WHEN DUE:
I am liable for the payment of the account of the facility and I am obligated to pay the account of the facility, in accordance with the regular rates and terms of the facility. If my injury is work-related, I 
am further obligated to pay the account of the facility in the event my employer or its third-party administrator denies payment for workers compensation. It is understood that the uninsured portion of 
bills are payable at the end of each week and in full upon discharge from the facility. I understand that after reasonable notice, delinquent accounts may be turned over to a collection agency and/or an 
attorney for collection. Should it be necessary to place this account in the hands of an attorney for collection, I agree to pay the costs of collection, including any court costs and a reasonable fee to the 
attorney employed by the facility to collect the account.
I agree that the facility, its employees, agents, attorneys and collection agencies, may call the cell number I provide for any reason, including but not limited to inquiring about the status and collection of 
my account. I also expressly authorize that each of them may use any mechanism, including but not limited to automatic dialing, artificial and prerecorded voice systems.

XI. PATIENT BILL OF RIGHTS: I acknowledge that a copy of the Patient Bill of Rights has been made available to me.

History limited by: None

HPI Pt is a 39 yr/o male who presents with neck and back "strain" following an MVA at 0730. Pt was the restrained driver
of a vehicle who was rear ended while at stop by another vehicle driving ~10mph. He denies any airbag deployment, head injury, or LOC. Pt states that he felt lightheadedness at work while moving around, but denies current
lightheadedness, dizziness or visual disturabance. Pt reports he has a hx of transitional vertebrae that occasionally
flares with sciatic pain to R hip and leg. Denies any sciatica but states his low back actually stated to bother him a
couple days ago and so he has been doing "extra stretches at home." Pt denies any acute back pain, numbness,
tingling, bowel or bladder incontinence, weakness in extremities and states his "whole back just feels tight". Hx of hypothyroidism dx after sudden weight gain (Hashimoto's disease).

[DOB-614] - ED in AUD Emergency Department (continued)
Clinical Notes (continued)
Cervical Spine Strain
WHAT YOU SHOULD KNOW:
Cervical spine strain is when the tissues and muscles in your neck are stretched. It is called whiplash because it 
happens when your neck is quickly whipped forward and back. The pain may be sudden, or it may begin hours after 
the injury. Cervical spine strain is most commonly caused by a car accident or a contact sports injury.
INSTRUCTIONS:
Medicines: · NSAIDs help decrease swelling and pain or fever. This medicine is available with or without a doctor's order. 
NSAIDs can cause stomach bleeding or kidney problems in certain people. If you take blood thinner medicine, 
always ask your healthcare provider if NSAIDs are safe for you. Always read the medicine label and follow 
directions. · Acetaminophen: This medicine decreases pain. It is available without a doctor's order. Ask how much to take 
and how often to take it. Follow directions. Acetaminophen can cause liver damage if not taken correctly. · Pain medicine: You may be given medicine to take away or decrease pain. Do not wait until the pain is severe 
before you take your medicine. · Muscle relaxers: This medicine helps relax your muscles. It is also given to decrease pain and muscle spasms.

Clinical Notes (continued) · Take your medicine as directed. Call your healthcare provider if you think your medicine is not helping or if
you have side effects. Tell him if you are allergic to any medicine. Keep a list of the medicines, vitamins, and
herbs you take. Include the amounts, and when and why you take them. Bring the list or the pill bottles to follow- up visits. Carry your medicine list with you in case of an emergency. Soft collar: You may need to wear a soft cervical collar to support your neck and hold it still. You may need to wear
this collar for 7 to 10 days. By day 3, your primary healthcare provider may tell you to take the collar off for short
periods of time. He may tell you to wear the collar less each day until you no longer need it. Self-care: · Rest: Avoid moving your neck as your injury heals. This will help decrease the risk of more damage to your
neck. Gradually return to your normal activities. Stop if you have pain. Avoid activities that can cause more
damage to your neck, such as heavy lifting or strenuous exercise. · Ice: Ice your neck to help decrease swelling and pain. Put crushed ice in a plastic bag. Cover the ice bag with a
towel and place it on your neck for 15 to 20 minutes every hour. Do this for as many days as directed. · Heat: Apply heat to your neck for 15 to 20 minutes several times each day. You can alternate heat and ice to
help with your pain. · Sleep: Sleep without a pillow to help decrease pain. Instead of a pillow, you may roll a small towel tightly and
place it under your neck. A soft collar may also help you sleep. Physical therapy: You may need to see a physical therapist to teach you special exercises. These exercises help
improve movement and decrease pain. Physical therapy can also help improve strength and decrease your risk for
loss of function. Contact your primary healthcare provider if: · Your neck pain is getting worse. · You have questions or concerns about your condition or care. Return to the emergency department if: · You have pain, numbness, tingling, or weakness of your arms, legs, face, or scalp. · You have shortness of breath, a hoarse voice, or problems swallowing. © 2014 Truven Health Analytics Inc. Low Back Strain
WHAT YOU SHOULD KNOW:
Low back strain is an injury to your lower back muscles or tendons. Tendons are strong tissues that connect muscles 
to bones. The lower back supports most of your body weight and helps you move, twist, and bend.
INSTRUCTIONS:
Medicines: The following medicines may be ordered by your healthcare provider: · NSAIDs: These medicines decrease swelling, pain, and fever. NSAIDs are available without a doctor's order. 
Ask your primary healthcare provider which medicine is right for you. Ask how much to take and when to take it. 
Take as directed. NSAIDs can cause stomach bleeding and kidney problems if not taken correctly. · Muscle relaxers: This medicine helps relax your muscles. It is also given to decrease pain and muscle spasms. · Pain medicine: You may be given a prescription medicine to decrease pain. Do not wait until the pain is severe 
before you take this medicine. · Take your medicine as directed. Call your healthcare provider if you think your medicine is not helping or if 
you have side effects. Tell him if you are allergic to any medicine. Keep a list of the medicines, vitamins, and 
herbs you take. Include the amounts, and when and why you take them. Bring the list or the pill bottles to followup visits. Carry your medicine list with you in case of an emergency.

Clinical Notes (continued)
Self-care: · Rest: You may need to rest in bed after your injury. · Activity: Slowly start to increase your activity as the pain decreases, or as directed. · Ice: Ice helps decrease swelling and pain. Ice may also help prevent tissue damage. Use an ice pack or put
crushed ice in a plastic bag. Cover it with a towel and place it on your lower back for 15 to 20 minutes every hour
as directed. · Heat: Heat helps decrease pain and muscle spasms. Apply heat on your lower back for 20 to 30 minutes every
2 hours for as many days as directed. Prevent another low back strain: · Use correct body movements: 
¨ Bend at the hips and knees when you pick up objects. Do not bend from the waist. Use your leg muscles as
you lift the load. Do not use your back. Keep the object close to your chest as you lift it. Try not to twist or lift
anything above your waist. ¨ Change your position often when you stand for long periods of time. Rest one foot on a small box or footrest, and then switch to the other foot often. ¨ Try not to sit for long periods of time. When you do, sit in a straight-backed chair with your feet flat on the
floor.
¨ Never reach, pull, or push while you are sitting. · Exercise: Warm up before you exercise. Strengthen your back muscles. Ask about the best exercise plan for
you. · Maintain a healthy weight: Ask your primary healthcare provider how much you should weigh. Ask him to help
you create a weight loss plan if you are overweight. Follow up with your healthcare provider as directed: Write down your questions so you remember to ask them
during your visits. Contact your primary healthcare provider if: · You have a fever. Generated on 11/4/24 11:53 AM Page 167

effective for you. Motor Vehicle Accident
WHAT YOU SHOULD KNOW:
Motor vehicle accident (MVA) is one of the leading causes of emergency visits. You may be bruised and sore from the
impact of the crash or being thrown around the inside of the car. You may also have face, neck, or back pain. You may
have a bruise on your abdomen, chest, or neck from the seatbelt. You may also have pain in your knee, hip, or thigh if
your body hits the dash or the steering wheel. Muscle pain is commonly worse 1 to 2 days after the accident.
INSTRUCTIONS:
Medicines: · Pain medicine: You may be given medicine to take away or decrease pain. Do not wait until the pain is severe
before you take your medicine. · NSAIDs help decrease swelling and pain or fever. This medicine is available with or without a doctor's order. NSAIDs can cause stomach bleeding or kidney problems in certain people. If you take blood thinner medicine, always ask if NSAIDs are safe for you. Always read the medicine label and follow directions. Do not give these 
medicines to children under 6 months of age without direction from your child's doctor. · Take your medicine as directed. Call your healthcare provider if you think your medicine is not helping or if
you have side effects. Tell him if you are allergic to any medicine. Keep a list of the medicines, vitamins, and
herbs you take. Include the amounts, and when and why you take them. Bring the list or the pill bottles to follow- Generated on 11/4/24 11:53 AM Page 168

Clinical Notes (continued)
up visits. Carry your medicine list with you in case of an emergency. Follow up with your healthcare provider as directed: Write down your questions so you remember to ask them
during your visits. Safety tips: · Always wear your seatbelt: This will help reduce injury from an MVA. · Use child safety seats: Your child needs to ride in a child safety seat made for his age, height, and weight. Ask
your primary healthcare provider for more information about child safety seats. · Decrease speed: Drive the speed limit to reduce your risk of an MVA. · Do not drive if you are tired: You will react more slowly when you are tired, and the slowed reaction time will
increase your chance of an MVA. · Do not talk or text on your cell phone while you drive: You cannot respond fast enough in an emergency if
you are distracted by texts or conversations. · Do not drink and drive: Use a designated driver. Call a taxi or get a ride home with someone if you have been
drinking. Do not let your friends drive if they have been drinking alcohol. · Do not use illegal drugs and drive: You may be more tired or take risks that you normally would not take. Also, do not drive after you take prescription medicines that make you sleepy. Self care: · Use ice and heat: Ice helps decrease swelling and pain. Ice may also help prevent tissue damage. Put crushed
ice in a plastic bag and cover it with a towel. Put the ice pack on your injured area for 15 to 20 minutes every
hour. Use the ice as directed. After 2 days, use a heating pad on your injured area. Use heat as directed. · Gently stretch: Use gentle exercises to stretch your muscles after an MVA. Ask your primary healthcare
provider for exercises you can do. Contact your primary healthcare provider if: · You have pain that develops 2 to 3 days after the MVA. · You have questions about your condition or care. Return to the emergency department if: · You have nausea and vomiting that does get better. Generated on 11/4/24 11:53 AM Page 169

information, medications, immunizations, allergies and more. You can even request appointments. To sign

appears below to complete the sign-up process. If you do not sign up before the expiration date, you must
request a new code. MyChart Access Code: MFMAY-6YK3T-74QUH

medical students, and students of various health care fields may be involved in my care and that they are not employees of the facility. I agree that the signing of this document does not in any way
imply that Norton Healthcare is responsible for or assumes any liability for the activities of any such physicians or practitioners who are not its employees. ED Provider Note
History
Chief Complaint
Patient presents with
• Motor Vehicle Crash
Got hit at a stop light approx 1700 today
• Neck Pain
had head turned Lt when getting hit and hit head rest. restrained driver
The history is provided by the patient. Time: 11:42 PM
Date: 7/12/2015
CC: Neck pain
Room: 5
HPI:
Context: Pt is a 39 yr/o male who presents to the ED for evaluation of neck pain, onset approx 1700 earlier today s/p
an MVC. The pt was the restrained driver of a vehicle which was rear-ended while at an intersection. There was
minimal damage to the vehicle; he claims that it was drive-able after the incident. At the time, the pt had his head
turned to the left side; he admits that his head slammed against his headrest during the MVC, and he has been
suffering mild left lateral neck pain ever since. In April 2015, the pt underwent another MVC and was experiencing
neck pain, which he describes as "whiplash." He also notes that he does have some minimal, left-sided pain in his
trunk and LUE. after that collision, he was evaluated at an ER, and had both X-rays and a CT of his C spine
performed, all of which were purportedly normal. At this time, the pt states that he is taking meds for his h/o
hypothyroidism. In several days, the pt has an appointment with a spine specialist, which he intends to go to after he
sees his PCP. There are no other complaints at this time.

[DOB-682] - ED in AUD Emergency Department (continued)
Clinical Notes (continued)
Cervical Spine Strain
WHAT YOU SHOULD KNOW:
Cervical spine strain is when the tissues and muscles in your neck are stretched. It is called whiplash because it
happens when your neck is quickly whipped forward and back. The pain may be sudden, or it may begin hours after
the injury. Cervical spine strain is most commonly caused by a car accident or a contact sports injury. AFTER YOU LEAVE:
Medicines: · NSAIDs help decrease swelling and pain or fever. This medicine is available with or without a doctor's order. NSAIDs can cause stomach bleeding or kidney problems in certain people. If you take blood thinner medicine, always ask your primary healthcare provider if NSAIDs are safe for you. Always read the medicine label and
follow directions. · Acetaminophen: This medicine decreases pain. It is available without a doctor's order. Ask how much to take
and how often to take it. Follow directions. Acetaminophen can cause liver damage if not taken correctly. · Pain medicine: 
You may need medicine to take away or decrease pain. ¨ Learn how to take your medicine. Ask what medicine and how much you should take. Be sure you know how, when, and how often to take it. ¨ Do not wait until the pain is severe before you take your medicine. Tell caregivers if your pain does not
decrease.
¨ Pain medicine can make you dizzy or sleepy. Prevent falls by calling someone when you get out of bed or if
you need help. · Muscle relaxers: This medicine helps relax your muscles. It is also given to decrease pain and muscle spasms. · Take your medicine as directed. Call your primary healthcare provider if you think your medicine is not helping
or if you have side effects. Tell him if you are allergic to any medicine. Keep a list of the medicines, vitamins, and
herbs you take. Include the amounts, and when and why you take them. Bring the list or the pill bottles to follow- up visits. Carry your medicine list with you in case of an emergency. Soft collar: You may need to wear a soft cervical collar to support your neck and hold it still. You may need to wear
this collar for 7 to 10 days. By day 3, your primary healthcare provider may tell you to take the collar off for short
periods of time. He may tell you to wear the collar less each day until you no longer need it. Generated on 11/4/24 11:53 AM Page 211
J.KIPER-M-001838

NORTON AUDUBON 
HOSPITAL
1 Audubon Plaza Drive
Louisville KY 40217-1318
Kiper, James
MRN: EP00479698, DOB: 4/29/1976, Sex: M
Acct #: 108509671
Adm: 7/12/2015, D/C: 7/12/2015
[DOB-683] - ED in AUD Emergency Department (continued)
Clinical Notes (continued)
Self-care: · Rest: Avoid moving your neck as your injury heals. This will help decrease the risk of more damage to your 
neck. Gradually return to your normal activities. Stop if you have pain. Avoid activities that can cause more 
damage to your neck, such as heavy lifting or strenuous exercise. · Ice: Ice your neck to help decrease swelling and pain. Put crushed ice in a plastic bag. Cover the ice bag with a 
towel and place it on your neck for 15 to 20 minutes every hour. Do this for as many days as directed. · Sleep: Sleep without a pillow to help decrease pain. Instead of a pillow, you may roll a small towel tightly and 
place it under your neck.
Physical therapy: You may need to see a physical therapist to teach you special exercises. These exercises help 
improve movement and decrease pain. Physical therapy can also help improve strength and decrease your risk for 
loss of function.
Contact your primary healthcare provider if: · Your neck pain is getting worse. · You have questions or concerns about your condition or care.
Seek care immediately or call 911 if: · You have pain, numbness, tingling, or weakness of your arms, face, or scalp. · You have shortness of breath, a hoarse voice, or problems swallowing.

[DOB-693] - ED in AUD Emergency Department (continued)
After Visit Summary (continued)
Discharge Instructions
Alternate Tylenol and ibuprofen as needed for pain. Apply either a heating pad or a cool ice pack to your neck as
needed. 
Go to your appointment with your primary care physician, and then your appointment with the spine specialist, as
previously scheduled. Also, follow up with your primary care physician for further re-checks, and further management, of your blood
pressure. 
Return to the ER if you develop any other new or worsening symptoms. Cervical Spine Strain
WHAT YOU SHOULD KNOW:
Cervical spine strain is when the tissues and muscles in your neck are stretched. It is called whiplash because it
happens when your neck is quickly whipped forward and back. The pain may be sudden, or it may begin hours after
the injury. Cervical spine strain is most commonly caused by a car accident or a contact sports injury. AFTER YOU LEAVE:
Medicines: · NSAIDs help decrease swelling and pain or fever. This medicine is available with or without a doctor's order. NSAIDs can cause stomach bleeding or kidney problems in certain people. If you take blood thinner medicine, always ask your primary healthcare provider if NSAIDs are safe for you. Always read the medicine label and
follow directions. · Acetaminophen: This medicine decreases pain. It is available without a doctor's order. Ask how much to take
and how often to take it. Follow directions. Acetaminophen can cause liver damage if not taken correctly. · Pain medicine: 
You may need medicine to take away or decrease pain. ¨ Learn how to take your medicine. Ask what medicine and how much you should take. Be sure you know how, when, and how often to take it. ¨ Do not wait until the pain is severe before you take your medicine. Tell caregivers if your pain does not
decrease.
¨ Pain medicine can make you dizzy or sleepy. Prevent falls by calling someone when you get out of bed or if
you need help. · Muscle relaxers: This medicine helps relax your muscles. It is also given to decrease pain and muscle spasms. Generated on 11/4/24 11:53 AM Page 220
J.KIPER-M-001847

NORTON AUDUBON 
HOSPITAL
1 Audubon Plaza Drive
Louisville KY 40217-1318
Kiper, James
MRN: EP00479698, DOB: 4/29/1976, Sex: M
Acct #: 108509671
Adm: 7/12/2015, D/C: 7/12/2015
[DOB-694] - ED in AUD Emergency Department (continued)
After Visit Summary (continued) · Take your medicine as directed. Call your primary healthcare provider if you think your medicine is not helping 
or if you have side effects. Tell him if you are allergic to any medicine. Keep a list of the medicines, vitamins, and 
herbs you take. Include the amounts, and when and why you take them. Bring the list or the pill bottles to followup visits. Carry your medicine list with you in case of an emergency.
Soft collar: You may need to wear a soft cervical collar to support your neck and hold it still. You may need to wear 
this collar for 7 to 10 days. By day 3, your primary healthcare provider may tell you to take the collar off for short 
periods of time. He may tell you to wear the collar less each day until you no longer need it.
Self-care: · Rest: Avoid moving your neck as your injury heals. This will help decrease the risk of more damage to your 
neck. Gradually return to your normal activities. Stop if you have pain. Avoid activities that can cause more 
damage to your neck, such as heavy lifting or strenuous exercise. · Ice: Ice your neck to help decrease swelling and pain. Put crushed ice in a plastic bag. Cover the ice bag with a 
towel and place it on your neck for 15 to 20 minutes every hour. Do this for as many days as directed. · Sleep: Sleep without a pillow to help decrease pain. Instead of a pillow, you may roll a small towel tightly and 
place it under your neck.
Physical therapy: You may need to see a physical therapist to teach you special exercises. These exercises help 
improve movement and decrease pain. Physical therapy can also help improve strength and decrease your risk for 
loss of function.
Contact your primary healthcare provider if: · Your neck pain is getting worse. · You have questions or concerns about your condition or care.

AUTHORIZATION FOR TREATMENT □ Kosair Children's Hospital □ Norton Hospital □ Norton Audubon Hospital □ Norton Women’s and Children’s Hospital □ Norton Brownsboro Hospital □ Kosair Children’s Medical Center
I. CONSENT TO DIAGNOSTIC TESTS, PROCEDURES, AND MEDICAL TREATMENT: 
I voluntarily consent to care that involves routine diagnostic tests, procedures, and medical treatment as prescribed by my physician and performed by the facility. No guarantee has been given by 
anyone as to the results that may be obtained. This consent includes testing for Hepatitis, Human Immunodeficiency Virus (HIV) or any other blood-borne infectious diseases, if ordered for diagnostic 
purposes or due to an occupational exposure. I consent to photographing, videotaping, video monitoring and audio devices for medical, scientific, safety or education purposes as well as for the 
purposes of identification. I understand that these will be stored in a secure manner that will protect my privacy. Images that identify me will only be released when authorized by me or as needed to 
provide for my continued medical treatment or identification.
II. OTHER PRACTITIONERS AND SUPPLIERS OF SERVICES:
I understand and acknowledge that I may require the services of physicians, groups of physicians or other practitioners (such as nurses and physician assistants) who are not employees of the facility,
including, but not limited to, anesthesiologists, radiologists, emergency department physicians, certified registered nurse anesthetists, and other practitioners. I also understand that residents, fellows,
medical students, and students of various health care fields may be involved in my care and that they are not employees of the facility. I agree that the signing of this document does not in any way
imply that Norton Healthcare is responsible for or assumes any liability for the activities of any such physicians or practitioners who are not its employees. When a physician, other practitioner or supplier of services bills me directly, I agree to pay the bill. I agree that the provisions regarding the release of information and assignment of benefits set out in paragraphs III and V below shall apply
not only to the facility but also to such physicians, practitioners and suppliers of services and their claims for payment.
III. RELEASE OF INFORMATION:
I authorize the facility to notify my referring and treating physician(s), of my admission to the facility and to release any information about me as requested by such physician(s). I authorize the facility
and any other holder of medical or other information about me including medical information concerning drug related conditions, alcoholism, psychological conditions, psychiatric conditions, and/or
blood-borne infectious diseases, to release to the Social Security Administration, its intermediaries and its carriers, State agencies, the review organization employed by my employer, or the employer of
the insured member of my family, or any private third-party payor, as appropriate, any information required for the completion of any claim for benefits arising out of services rendered to me either on
an inpatient or outpatient basis. I further authorize the release of my social security number to the manufacturer of any implanted medical device in accordance with the Medical Device Tracking Act of
the Food and Drug Administration (FDA). I authorize the release of my HIV test results to healthcare personnel in the event of an occupational exposure. If my injury is work-related, I authorize the
facility and any other holder of medical or other information about me to release from my medical record any information as requested by the company and/or its workers compensation administrator as
indicated below:

am further obligated to pay the account of the facility in the event my employer or its third-party administrator denies payment for workers compensation. It is understood that the uninsured portion of 
bills are payable at the end of each week and in full upon discharge from the facility. I understand that after reasonable notice, delinquent accounts may be turned over to a collection agency and/or an 
attorney for collection. Should it be necessary to place this account in the hands of an attorney for collection, I agree to pay the costs of collection, including any court costs and a reasonable fee to the 
attorney employed by the facility to collect the account.
I agree that the facility, its employees, agents, attorneys and collection agencies, may call the cell number I provide for any reason, including but not limited to inquiring about the status and collection of 
my account. I also expressly authorize that each of them may use any mechanism, including but not limited to automatic dialing, artificial and prerecorded voice systems.

MyChart Activation
MyChart allows you to view portions of your electronic medical record. If you have a Norton Healthcare
primary care physician, you can send messages to your doctor's office, view lab results and appointment
information, medications, immunizations, allergies and more. You can even request appointments. To sign
up, log on to https://mychart.nortonhealthcare.org. Once you are logged on, click on the Sign Up Now
link and you will access the new member sign-up page. Enter your MyChart Access Code exactly as it
appears below to complete the sign-up process. If you do not sign up before the expiration date, you must
request a new code. MyChart Access Code: Activation code not generated
Current MyChart Status: Active
If you are a parent or legal guardian and want access to your child's MyChart account, or if you are the
authorized caregiver for another person and want proxy access to their MyChart account, please email the
request to [EMAIL-810]. 
If you have other questions, you can email [EMAIL-811] or call [PHONE-812]. Remember, MyChart is NOT to be used for urgent needs. For medical emergencies, dial 911.

Clinical Notes
Hemorrhoids
WHAT YOU NEED TO KNOW:
Hemorrhoids are swollen blood vessels inside your rectum (internal hemorrhoids) or on your anus (external 
hemorrhoids). Sometimes a hemorrhoid may prolapse, which means it extends out of your anus.

[DOB-886] - ED in AUD Emergency Department (continued)
Clinical Notes (continued)
DISCHARGE INSTRUCTIONS:
Return to the emergency department if: · You have severe pain in your rectum or around your anus. · You have bleeding from your anus that does not stop.
Contact your healthcare provider if: · You have frequent and painful bowel movements. · You see blood in the toilet bowl or on the toilet paper after a bowel movement. · You have questions or concerns about your condition or care.
Medicines: · Medicines can help decrease pain and swelling, and soften your bowel movement. The medicine may be a pill, 
pad, cream, or ointment. · Take your medicine as directed. Call your healthcare provider if you think your medicine is not helping or if 
you have side effects. Tell him if you are allergic to any medicine. Keep a list of the medicines, vitamins, and 
herbs you take. Include the amounts, and when and why you take them. Bring the list or the pill bottles to followup visits. Carry your medicine list with you in case of an emergency.
Manage your symptoms: · Apply ice on your anus for 15 to 20 minutes every hour or as directed. Use an ice pack, or put crushed ice in a

[DOB-887] - ED in AUD Emergency Department (continued)
Clinical Notes (continued)
plastic bag. Cover it with a towel. Ice helps prevent tissue damage and decreases swelling and pain. · Take a sitz bath. Fill a bathtub with 4 to 6 inches of warm water. You may also use a sitz bath pan that fits over 
a toilet. Sit in the sitz bath for 20 minutes. Do this 2 to 3 times a day, or as directed. The warm water can help 
decrease pain and swelling. · Keep your anal area clean. Gently wash the area with warm water daily. Soap may irritate the area. After a 
bowel movement, wipe with moist towelettes or wet toilet paper. Dry toilet paper can irritate the area.
Prevent hemorrhoids: · Do not strain to have a bowel movement or sit on the toilet too long. · Prevent constipation and soften your bowel movement. Exercise, such as walking, may make it easier to 
have a bowel movement. Drink liquids as directed. Ask how much liquid to drink each day and which liquids are 
best for you. Eat a variety of high fiber foods, including fruits, vegetables, and whole grains.
· Avoid anal sex. It can weaken the skin around your rectum and anus.
Follow up with your healthcare provider as directed: Write down your questions so you remember to ask them 
during your visits.

[DOB-909] - ED in AUD Emergency Department (continued)
After Visit Summary (continued)
Discharge Instructions
Hemorrhoids
WHAT YOU NEED TO KNOW:
Hemorrhoids are swollen blood vessels inside your rectum (internal hemorrhoids) or on your anus (external 
hemorrhoids). Sometimes a hemorrhoid may prolapse, which means it extends out of your anus. 
DISCHARGE INSTRUCTIONS:
Return to the emergency department if: · You have severe pain in your rectum or around your anus. · You have bleeding from your anus that does not stop.
Contact your healthcare provider if: · You have frequent and painful bowel movements. · You see blood in the toilet bowl or on the toilet paper after a bowel movement. · You have questions or concerns about your condition or care.
Medicines: · Medicines can help decrease pain and swelling, and soften your bowel movement. The medicine may be a pill, 
pad, cream, or ointment.

[DOB-910] - ED in AUD Emergency Department (continued)
After Visit Summary (continued) · Take your medicine as directed. Call your healthcare provider if you think your medicine is not helping or if 
you have side effects. Tell him if you are allergic to any medicine. Keep a list of the medicines, vitamins, and 
herbs you take. Include the amounts, and when and why you take them. Bring the list or the pill bottles to followup visits. Carry your medicine list with you in case of an emergency.
Manage your symptoms: · Apply ice on your anus for 15 to 20 minutes every hour or as directed. Use an ice pack, or put crushed ice in a 
plastic bag. Cover it with a towel. Ice helps prevent tissue damage and decreases swelling and pain. · Take a sitz bath. Fill a bathtub with 4 to 6 inches of warm water. You may also use a sitz bath pan that fits over 
a toilet. Sit in the sitz bath for 20 minutes. Do this 2 to 3 times a day, or as directed. The warm water can help 
decrease pain and swelling. · Keep your anal area clean. Gently wash the area with warm water daily. Soap may irritate the area. After a 
bowel movement, wipe with moist towelettes or wet toilet paper. Dry toilet paper can irritate the area.
Prevent hemorrhoids: · Do not strain to have a bowel movement or sit on the toilet too long. · Prevent constipation and soften your bowel movement. Exercise, such as walking, may make it easier to 
have a bowel movement. Drink liquids as directed. Ask how much liquid to drink each day and which liquids are 
best for you. Eat a variety of high fiber foods, including fruits, vegetables, and whole grains.
· Avoid anal sex. It can weaken the skin around your rectum and anus.
Follow up with your healthcare provider as directed: Write down your questions so you remember to ask them

After Visit Summary (continued)
Discharge Instructions
Hemorrhoids
WHAT YOU NEED TO KNOW:
Hemorrhoids are swollen blood vessels inside your rectum (internal hemorrhoids) or on your anus (external 
hemorrhoids). Sometimes a hemorrhoid may prolapse, which means it extends out of your anus. 
DISCHARGE INSTRUCTIONS:
Return to the emergency department if: · You have severe pain in your rectum or around your anus. · You have bleeding from your anus that does not stop.
Contact your healthcare provider if: · You have frequent and painful bowel movements. · You see blood in the toilet bowl or on the toilet paper after a bowel movement. · You have questions or concerns about your condition or care.
Medicines: · Medicines can help decrease pain and swelling, and soften your bowel movement. The medicine may be a pill, 
pad, cream, or ointment.

[DOB-921] - ED in AUD Emergency Department (continued)
After Visit Summary (continued) · Take your medicine as directed. Call your healthcare provider if you think your medicine is not helping or if 
you have side effects. Tell him if you are allergic to any medicine. Keep a list of the medicines, vitamins, and 
herbs you take. Include the amounts, and when and why you take them. Bring the list or the pill bottles to followup visits. Carry your medicine list with you in case of an emergency.
Manage your symptoms: · Apply ice on your anus for 15 to 20 minutes every hour or as directed. Use an ice pack, or put crushed ice in a 
plastic bag. Cover it with a towel. Ice helps prevent tissue damage and decreases swelling and pain. · Take a sitz bath. Fill a bathtub with 4 to 6 inches of warm water. You may also use a sitz bath pan that fits over 
a toilet. Sit in the sitz bath for 20 minutes. Do this 2 to 3 times a day, or as directed. The warm water can help 
decrease pain and swelling. · Keep your anal area clean. Gently wash the area with warm water daily. Soap may irritate the area. After a 
bowel movement, wipe with moist towelettes or wet toilet paper. Dry toilet paper can irritate the area.
Prevent hemorrhoids: · Do not strain to have a bowel movement or sit on the toilet too long. · Prevent constipation and soften your bowel movement. Exercise, such as walking, may make it easier to 
have a bowel movement. Drink liquids as directed. Ask how much liquid to drink each day and which liquids are 
best for you. Eat a variety of high fiber foods, including fruits, vegetables, and whole grains.
· Avoid anal sex. It can weaken the skin around your rectum and anus.
Follow up with your healthcare provider as directed: Write down your questions so you remember to ask them

Colonoscopy Procedure Note
James R Kiper
4/29/1976
male
EP00479698
4/12/2017
Pre-operative Diagnosis: Rectal pain and pressure
Post-operative Diagnosis: same
Procedure: Colonoscopy --diagnostic
Surgeon: Gregory B. Strothman, MD
Indications: Rectal pain and pressure
Sedation: MAC
Procedure Details:
Informed consent was obtained for the procedure, including sedation. Risks of bowel injury and hemorrhage were
discussed.The patient was monitored continuously with ECG tracing, pulse oximetry, blood pressure monitoring, and
direct observations. The patient was placed in the left lateral decubitus position. He was given intravenous sedation by
anesthesia. A digital rectal examination was performed. The variable-stiffness colonoscope was inserted into the
rectum and advanced under direct vision to the cecum, which was identified by the ileocecal valve and appendiceal
orifice. The quality of the colonic preparation was good. A careful inspection was made as the colonoscope was
withdrawn, including a retroflexed view of the rectum. Findings and interventions are described below. Findings:
-normal colonic mucosa throughout
Specimens: none
 Complications: None; patient tolerated the procedure well. Recommendations:
-For colon cancer screening in this average-risk patient, colonoscopy may be repeated in 10 years. Gregory B. Strothman, MD
4/12/2017
9:01 AM

Patient Education
Title: PreOp/PostOp Surgery - OutPatient ()
Topic: Discharge Planning - OP Surgery (Resolved)
You and your care team will work together to make sure you are ready to go home when you are getting
better. Please be planning who can pick you up from the hospital so finding transportation does not delay
you going home. Many things need to be completed before you can go home. It may take several hours
once you know you are going home until the time you are ready to leave the hospital. Use this time to make
sure you have all the information and know how to do all the medical care needed at home. Also begin
gathering all items you need to take back home.
Topic: Health and Safety (Resolved)
Patients or patient's guardians have a right to voice safety concerns related to care and environment. Please talk to the unit staff and a nurse leader. If you still have concerns, you may dial 0 and ask to speak
to the administrator on call.
Point: Discharge Instructions - Will Get Written Discharge Instructions (Resolved)
will be provided, review the role of the home care nurse and
when to expect the first visit. Provide written instructions as indicated. Explain to family that they should prepare the home environment for safety/falls prevention if indicated (minimize trip hazards, keep areas well lit, avoid slippery, wet floors, etc). Use caution near pets (pets can be a tripping hazard).
If the patient has an incision instruct them to not allow pets to get near the incision so as to decrease the chance of infection.
Point: Assist Patient/Family/Caregiver to Prepare for Discharge (Resolved)
Point: Reporting Safety Issues (Resolved)
Description:
Educate patient/family/caregiver on discharge instructions. Review the physician's discharge instructions with patient and
primary caregiver including follow-up appointments, diet, activity, medications and special precautions. If home care
services

Patient Education (continued)
You should let the healthcare team know if you are concerned with any changes in the patient's condition. If
you remain concerned and do not think everything is being done – you have the option to call the Rapid
Response Team. A team of trained staff will come to the patient's bedside to check on them. DIAL 3333
and tell them you need the Rapid Response Team. Tell them the patient's name and room number.
Germs are spread when you cough or sneeze. Please try to “cover your cough.” Cover your mouth and
nose with a tissue and throw away the tissue. If you do not have a tissue, cover your mouth and nose with
the bend or crook of your arm at your elbow. Wash your hands often.

[DOB-1038] - Admission (Discharged) in AUD Endoscopy (continued)
Patient Education (continued)
Clean your hands often with soap and clean water or use an alcohol based hand sanitizer to help prevent
the spread of germs. Always clean your hands before and after doing any care, making food or eating food, and using the bathroom.
The hospital environment is different from your home. Help us keep you and your loved ones safe from falls. 
Ask for help before getting out of bed. Ask how many side rails should stay up at all times. Wear footwear
that will not slip on the floors. Keep the room free from clutter. Some patients may use a bed alarm for their
safety that will alert staff if the patient is trying to get out of bed.
Tobacco smoke can be harmful to all. To help us protect all patients and guest, all areas of Norton
Healthcare and our campuses are smoke free and vape free. Smoking and vaping are not allowed.
Have them demonstrate proper hand washing technique using soap, water, friction, clean nails under running water, and dry
hands on clean towel without touching dirty surfaces and using alcohol based decontaminates.
Point: Falls Precautions (Resolved) * Instruct to call for help before getting out of bed
* Instruct to wear non-slip footwear when out of bed
* Instruct why they are at risk for falling
* Communicate "at risk" status with patient and family
* If discharging home, instruct on home modifications to reduce falls in the home
Point: Latex Precautions as Appropriate (Resolved)
Point: Hazards of Environmental Tobacco Smoke (Resolved)
Description:

important step in preventing the spread of germs. Patient Friendly Description:

 CONDITIONS OF ADMISSION AND 
AUTHORIZATION FOR TREATMENT □ Norton Children's Hospital □ Norton Hospital □ Norton Audubon Hospital □ Norton Women’s and Children’s Hospital □ Norton Brownsboro Hospital □ Norton Children’s Medical Center
I. CONSENT TO DIAGNOSTIC TESTS, PROCEDURES, AND MEDICAL TREATMENT: 
I voluntarily consent to care that involves routine diagnostic tests, procedures, and medical treatment as prescribed by my physician and performed by the facility. No guarantee has been given by 
anyone as to the results that may be obtained. This consent includes testing for Hepatitis, Human Immunodeficiency Virus (HIV) or any other blood-borne infectious diseases, if ordered for diagnostic 
purposes or due to an occupational exposure. I consent to photographing, videotaping, video monitoring and audio devices for medical, scientific, safety or education purposes as well as for the 
purposes of identification. I understand that these will be stored in a secure manner that will protect my privacy. Images that identify me will only be released when authorized by me or as needed to 
provide for my continued medical treatment or identification.
II. OTHER PRACTITIONERS AND SUPPLIERS OF SERVICES:
I understand and acknowledge that I may require the services of physicians, groups of physicians or other practitioners (such as nurses and physician assistants) who are not employees of the facility,
including, but not limited to, anesthesiologists, radiologists, emergency department physicians, certified registered nurse anesthetists, and other practitioners. I also understand that residents, fellows,
medical students, and students of various health care fields may be involved in my care and that they are not employees of the facility. I agree that the signing of this document does not in any way
imply that Norton Healthcare is responsible for or assumes any liability for the activities of any such physicians or practitioners who are not its employees. When a physician, other practitioner or supplier of services bills me directly, I agree to pay the bill. I agree that the provisions regarding the release of information and assignment of benefits set out in paragraphs III and V below shall apply
not only to the facility but also to such physicians, practitioners and suppliers of services and their claims for payment.
III. RELEASE OF INFORMATION:
I authorize the facility to notify my referring and treating physician(s), of my admission to the facility and to release any information about me as requested by such physician(s). I authorize the facility
and any other holder of medical or other information about me including medical information concerning drug related conditions, alcoholism, psychological conditions, psychiatric conditions, and/or
blood-borne infectious diseases, to release to the Social Security Administration, its intermediaries and its carriers, State agencies, the review organization employed by my employer, or the employer of
the insured member of my family, or any private third-party payor, as appropriate, any information required for the completion of any claim for benefits arising out of services rendered to me either on
an inpatient or outpatient basis. I further authorize the release of my social security number to the manufacturer of any implanted medical device in accordance with the Medical Device Tracking Act of
the Food and Drug Administration (FDA). I authorize the release of my HIV test results to healthcare personnel in the event of an occupational exposure. If my injury is work-related, I authorize the
facility and any other holder of medical or other information about me to release from my medical record any information as requested by the company and/or its workers compensation administrator as
indicated below:
COMPANY________________________________________________________________________ ADDRESS__________________________________________
IV. (initial)
THE FACILITY IS NOT RESPONSIBLE FOR LOSS OF

V. ASSIGNMENT OF BENEFITS:

document shall remain in full force and effect until specifically revoked by me in writing. Any sums not paid by a third-party payor are my obligation.
VI. RELEASE OF INSURANCE INFORMATION TO FACILITY:
I agree to the release by my insurance carrier to the facility and the facility's billing service of any eligibility and utilization data concerning my insurance coverage which the facility and/or its billing 
supplier may require. I authorize the facility to file an appeal of a payment denial and/or request a hearing regarding any denial of payment for treatment provided to me. I further authorize the facility 
to present proof, utilize facility records and my records and documentation for appeals and hearings.
VII. PAYMENT OF FACILITY BILLS WHEN DUE:
I am liable for the payment of the account of the facility and I am obligated to pay the account of the facility, in accordance with the regular rates and terms of the facility. If my injury is work-related, I 
am further obligated to pay the account of the facility in the event my employer or its third-party administrator denies payment for workers compensation. It is understood that the uninsured portion of 
bills are payable at the end of each week and in full upon discharge from the facility. I understand that after reasonable notice, delinquent accounts may be turned over to a collection agency and/or an 
attorney for collection. Should it be necessary to place this account in the hands of an attorney for collection, I agree to pay the costs of collection, including any court costs and a reasonable fee to the 
attorney employed by the facility to collect the account.
I agree that the facility, its employees, agents, attorneys and collection agencies, may call the cell number I provide for any reason, including but not limited to inquiring about the status and collection of 
my account. I also expressly authorize that each of them may use any mechanism, including but not limited to automatic dialing, artificial and prerecorded voice systems.

XI. PATIENT BILL OF RIGHTS: I acknowledge that a copy of the Patient Bill of Rights has been made available to me.

I. CONSENT TO DIAGNOSTIC TESTS, PROCEDURES, AND MEDICAL TREATMENT: 
I voluntarily consent to care that involves routine diagnostic tests, procedures, and medical treatment as prescribed by my physician and performed by the facility. No guarantee has been given by 
anyone as to the results that may be obtained. This consent includes testing for Hepatitis, Human Immunodeficiency Virus (HIV) or any other blood-borne infectious diseases, if ordered for diagnostic 
purposes or due to an occupational exposure. I consent to photographing, videotaping, video monitoring and audio devices for medical, scientific, safety or education purposes as well as for the 
purposes of identification. I understand that these will be stored in a secure manner that will protect my privacy. Images that identify me will only be released when authorized by me or as needed to 
provide for my continued medical treatment or identification.
II. OTHER PRACTITIONERS AND SUPPLIERS OF SERVICES:
I understand and acknowledge that I may require the services of physicians, groups of physicians or other practitioners (such as nurses and physician assistants) who are not employees of the facility, 
including, but not limited to, anesthesiologists, radiologists, emergency department physicians, certified registered nurse anesthetists, and other practitioners. I also understand that residents, fellows, 
medical students, and students of various health care fields may be involved in my care and that they are not employees of the facility. I agree that the signing of this document does not in any way 
imply that Norton Healthcare is responsible for or assumes any liability for the activities of any such physicians or practitioners who are not its employees. When a physician, other practitioner or 
supplier of services bills me directly, I agree to pay the bill. I agree that the provisions regarding the release of information and assignment of benefits set out in paragraphs III and V below shall apply 
not only to the facility but also to such physicians, practitioners and suppliers of services and their claims for payment.
III. RELEASE OF INFORMATION:
I authorize the facility to notify my referring and treating physician(s), of my admission to the facility and to release any information about me as requested by such physician(s). I authorize the facility 
and any other holder of medical or other information about me including medical information concerning drug related conditions, alcoholism, psychological conditions, psychiatric conditions, and/or 
blood-borne infectious diseases, to release to the Social Security Administration, its intermediaries and its carriers, State agencies, the review organization employed by my employer, or the employer of 
the insured member of my family, or any private third-party payor, as appropriate, any information required for the completion of any claim for benefits arising out of services rendered to me either on 
an inpatient or outpatient basis. I further authorize the release of my social security number to the manufacturer of any implanted medical device in accordance with the Medical Device Tracking Act of 
the Food and Drug Administration (FDA). I authorize the release of my HIV test results to healthcare personnel in the event of an occupational exposure. If my injury is work-related, I authorize the 
facility and any other holder of medical or other information about me to release from my medical record any information as requested by the company and/or its workers compensation administrator as 
indicated below:
COMPANY________________________________________________________________________ ADDRESS__________________________________________

I agree to the release by my insurance carrier to the facility and the facility's billing service of any eligibility and utilization data concerning my insurance coverage which the facility and/or its billing 
supplier may require. I authorize the facility to file an appeal of a payment denial and/or request a hearing regarding any denial of payment for treatment provided to me. I further authorize the facility 
to present proof, utilize facility records and my records and documentation for appeals and hearings.
VII. PAYMENT OF FACILITY BILLS WHEN DUE:
I am liable for the payment of the account of the facility and I am obligated to pay the account of the facility, in accordance with the regular rates and terms of the facility. If my injury is work-related, I am further obligated to pay the account of the facility in the event my employer or its third-party administrator denies payment for workers compensation. It is understood that the uninsured portion of
bills are payable at the end of each week and in full upon discharge from the facility. I understand that after reasonable notice, delinquent accounts may be turned over to a collection agency and/or an
attorney for collection. Should it be necessary to place this account in the hands of an attorney for collection, I agree to pay the costs of collection, including any court costs and a reasonable fee to the
attorney employed by the facility to collect the account.
I agree that the facility, its employees, agents, attorneys and collection agencies, may call the cell number I provide for any reason, including but not limited to inquiring about the status and collection of 
my account. I also expressly authorize that each of them may use any mechanism, including but not limited to automatic dialing, artificial and prerecorded voice systems.
